Standards for Civic Training in Elementary Schools (4)

5. Key Points of Implementation Plan

I. Civic training should be implemented in two aspects:

(1) Public training

(a) During teaching time for each subject, teachers should indirectly guide children or directly explain based on the outline items.

(b) At any time and place, teachers should pay attention to various activities of children, directly and indirectly cite regulations and various items, and guide children to abide by them.

(c) In a certain period, according to the public needs of children or when public shortcomings of children are discovered, select appropriate virtues as the center of training and use various methods for public training, lasting from one to two weeks.

(d) Every week, on Memorial Week, the entire school should read aloud or compose the meaning of the words into songs to sing. Each week, an appropriate virtue can also be selected for special emphasis and used as public training, but it should not be reduced to shouting slogans or posting slogans.

(e) During the sixty-minute specific time each week, divide the sixty minutes into three times, teaching every other day, or divide it into six times, guiding daily. During each specific time, the teacher should cite items based on occasional events and explain them. If a training week is held, emphasis should be placed on items related to the central virtue.

(2) Individual training can be divided into several groups or several teams, depending on the number of teachers and students in the school. Each teacher is responsible for the individual training of one group or one team, supervising them to practice the items in various ways, conducting self-examination, and paying attention to examining the results.

II. Each school should set up a civic training committee to jointly discuss and determine the organizational system and specific methods of civic training. All teachers must participate.

III. At the beginning of each semester, each school should divide the training items into stages and make small booklets or loose-leaf pages, which should be distributed to children by groups or teams so that children understand the matters that should be paid attention to in this semester and have the opportunity to reflect.

IV. The training items of each stage should be arranged in order by each school and divided into four small stages, evenly distributed to children in each grade for training for the four semesters.

V. Training items that each child can do should continue to be trained and examined later.

VI. Local competent educational administrative authorities may guide each school to appropriately increase or decrease stages or change them according to the actual needs of the training items.

VII. Teachers in each school should take the opportunity to jointly formulate items with children and discuss methods to achieve various items based on this standard using suggestive methods to avoid coercive methods.

VIII. In addition to teachers' usual observation and recording, each group or team should regularly conduct examinations weekly or monthly, make children reflect on or jointly criticize the training items, and use competitions and honorary awards to improve the efficiency of training.

IX. The results of the civic training examination should be compiled into children's reflection record forms, teacher observation record forms, a comparison table for each group or team, and reports to parents, so that teachers, students, and parents can clearly understand the results of civic training.

X. Civic training emphasizes practice and does not use textbooks.

XI. Civic training pays attention to personality influence, and teachers must set an example.

XII. The school environment should be appropriately arranged and equipped according to Chinese civic regulations, such as equipment that meets health principles, so that children can receive good environmental training unconsciously. XIII. Civic training should use more positive activities to subtly influence children and develop various good habits. Avoid using negative methods of suppression to create a hypocritical attitude where children are afraid to do something. XIV. Individual training is more important than public training. Therefore, the personality, ability, physical strength, family situation, and social environment of children related to civic training must be carefully examined and investigated. XV. Civic training must be linked to the family, so that parents report the characteristics of their children to the school, and the school regularly reports the examination results to parents to seek mutual cooperation.

XVI. Group organizations can provide training, such as self-government organizations and other group activities such as academics, health, art, and communication. Sufficient training opportunities should be given at any time.

XVII. Children in each grade should be allowed to participate in social activities at any time to help the progress of social undertakings, such as conducting fly eradication campaigns and household surveys.

XVIII. Higher grades should train children to investigate and judge the advantages and disadvantages of various undertakings in their own organizations and social environment and plan how to improve them. (End)

Establishment of Curriculum Compilation Committee for Kindergartens and Elementary Schools in This City

The Ministry of Education has officially promulgated the new curriculum standards for kindergartens and elementary schools. Recently, it also designated provinces such as Jiangsu and Zhejiang and cities such as Shanghai to organize curriculum compilation committees in accordance with Item 4 of the Implementation Measures for Curriculum Standards. It is learned that the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau has separately appointed educational experts, bureau staff, and teachers specializing in various subjects in elementary schools in this city to form the Kindergarten and Elementary School Curriculum Compilation Committee and has formulated rules and submitted them to the Municipal Government and the Ministry of Education for record. On the afternoon of the 23rd, a grand establishment meeting was held in the auditorium of the Education Bureau, attended by more than ten expert committee members, including Tao Baichuan, Jiang Xicen, Yang Pingyu, Lei Zhenqing, Ge Xianting, Han Mingyi, and Zong Lianghuan; more than ten bureau staff members, including Director Pan Gongzhan, Section Chief Zhou Feicheng, Hu Changcai, Supervisor Xie Engao, and Specialist Zhou Shang and Zhang Yongchun; and more than twenty city school principals and teachers, including Zhang Zhaoyun, Gong Jiajun, Zhao Luqing, Qian Xuanqing, and Zhong Zitong, totaling more than fifty people. The meeting was chaired by Director Pan, and after performing the ceremony, the chairman first reported the significance of the establishment of the committee, the preparation process, the importance of the work, and its steps, and introduced each expert committee member one by one, as well as hoped for the efforts of each committee member and thanked each expert for their enthusiastic cooperation. The meeting ended at 6:00 PM. The general outline of the work of the committee is recorded below: First step, compile the main items for each subject and each academic year in accordance with the standards promulgated by the Ministry, and collect the central units that have been implemented in various schools for reference by each group. This step of work is limited to be completed by the end of March. Second step, each group will combine the main items of each academic year into each central unit. This step of work is limited to be completed before April 20. Third step, compile the limits of achievement for each subject, limited to be completed in early May. Fourth step, compile teaching examples, limited to be completed by the end of May. Fifth step, review, limited to be completed before June 20. Sixth step, typesetting. Seventh step, submit to the Ministry of Education and the Municipal Government for approval, issue orders to various elementary schools for implementation, and designate several schools to report the test results within a limited time to facilitate modification.

Special Article: Several Hopes for Education in Zhejiang Province

I have several opinions and wishes for the education sector in Zhejiang Province and all parties related to education. At the beginning of this year, 1933, I will briefly state them.

1. I hope that those who serve education in this province will work hard at all times, be thrifty, invigorate themselves every day, and be excited to put into practice the wish of saving the country through education. You must know that a few hours of idle leisure and the waste of a piece of paper or a pen are incalculable losses in the midst of serious national crises.

2. I hope that educators will recognize the national situation of our country and truly recognize that our responsibility is not only to create individuals, but to create the citizens needed for the survival of our country. Anyone who only takes a formal acknowledgment of the purpose of education in the Republic of China and its implementation guidelines and cannot truly fulfill them can only be regarded as occasionally serving education, not the educator needed by the country.

III. I hope that the teachers and staff of middle and primary schools in this province will pay close attention to the students' studies and not make it seem on the surface that everything is available, decorated in colorful ways, while many parents frown when examining their children's studies and sigh, "It's not as good as it used to be." The low level of general students (even if not all) is, whatever the reason, a reality that cannot be avoided. Therefore, I sincerely hope that everyone will not talk about lofty ideals and show off new things, but based on true facts, present the facts that the students' studies can be explained.

IV. I hope that those who preside over mass education in this province will not just resent the indifference of society to mass education, the difficulty of funding, and the difficulty of progress. I believe that each county should not regard mass education as an order to be followed or as a decoration to be seen. Our mass education centers in each county should focus on one or several activities and work hard to attract everyone's attention. In places where education is backward, you must not give up on yourself and become a useless organization that only hangs a sign. In places with better economic and talent resources, you must not be greedy for too much and become too broad, which will result in the inability to produce a real result. You must not take means as the purpose, only to make it a place for public entertainment, but without any educational significance.

V. I hope that the county magistrates of each county will have more enthusiasm and concern for education. The development and prosperity of a county and the progress of various county policies are closely related to the rise and fall of education. Therefore, the leadership of the county's overall education plan and the promotion of education and learning are the responsibilities that enlightened county magistrates should take upon themselves.

VI. I hope that the directors of the Education Bureau in each county will be diligent and alert and seek the consolidation and development of local education amidst thousands of hardships. First, their own behavior must be strictly checked. Second, their attitude towards people must not be too frivolous, and the handling of affairs must not be too careless. Third, they must be able to endure grievances, withstand pressure, work hard and complain little, and be organized and methodical.

L. I hope that the parents of our Zhejiang students will no longer fail to pay attention to their children's character and studies, and no longer fail to plan their children's future in advance. Many young students who have parents who urge and teach them at any time will always achieve better results than those who do not have parents to discipline them. As for the issue of children's further education, it is especially a problem that should be seriously considered but is ignored by most parents. I think this is a big reason for the lack of direction of many young people. I believe that each parent should send their children to ordinary junior high schools without consideration, planning, or preparation when their children graduate from elementary school is not necessarily a way to love their children. At the time of graduation from junior high school, because there was no overall plan, it was the same haste and no consideration and preparation to send them to ordinary high school, thinking that they would let them pass four years and then say that this is especially likely to harm children. Because if the family cannot afford the tuition fees, then the result will inevitably be tragic, either the children and the family are not in harmony, or the children are forced to drop out of school due to family pressure and cannot find a suitable job. Because the number of people in Zhejiang who go to school is not small, I personally feel that this meaning is even more profound. I believe that each parent should carefully consider and plan the further education and employment of their children in advance. If the family's supply and the children's personality are suitable up to a certain stage, resolutely decide to let him drop out of school or change to various vocational and aesthetic training institutions for employment preparation, which is the parents' best way to love their children.

VIII. I hope that our Zhejiang elders and brothers will restore the spirit of the early schools more than 20 years ago to promote education in each county throughout our province. In the situation where the provincial funds are so difficult and the rural economy in each county is showing signs of collapse, what we should do, such as running vocational schools at all levels, promoting compulsory education, adding mass schools... etc., are all imminent and require considerable funding. We now have nothing else that can overcome difficulties, but to raise a heart of enthusiasm and solve the problems in education. If people in each county, each district, and each township do not rise up together to plan, and elders and brothers throughout the province help as much as possible, then the education and culture of Zhejiang will inevitably not progress. In order to seek the happiness of the compatriots in this province, we cannot but sincerely ask for the cooperation of the people in Zhejiang.

Chen Bulei

Municipal Education Bureau to Hold Wireless Broadcasting Tutoring Classes

| Subjects temporarily include Civics, Mandarin, and English |

Starts March 1st, 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM Every Night

The Municipal Education Bureau has been paying more attention to the active promotion of social education in the past six months. Recently, it is planning to use radio stations to hold wireless broadcasting tutoring classes so that generally older unemployed or semi-literate workers and apprentices can obtain the opportunity for remedial education. Leisure time will not be wasted, and the law is good and meaningful, which is really groundbreaking. It is learned that the radio tutoring class will start broadcasting programs from 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM every night from March 1 at the Hengsen Radio Station on Nanjing Road, divided into two subjects: [Civics] [Mandarin] [English]. The Bureau has consulted with the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and instructed various factories and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and various trade associations to inform various shops and companies and quickly equip them with radios and announce to workers and apprentices to abide by and register for learning. All those who wish to learn can directly register with the Municipal Education Bureau.

Shanghai Education Bureau Radio Broadcast Tutorial Class Regulations

1. In order to implement social education, popularize literacy, and promote sports, this bureau is establishing radio broadcast tutorial classes (hereinafter referred to as "radio tutorial classes") to provide general older, out-of-school, or slightly literate shop assistants, apprentices, and workers with the opportunity to use their spare time to obtain remedial education, enhance their knowledge, and adapt to social life.

2. Radio tutorial classes have no enrollment limit and do not charge tuition fees. Anyone who is willing to receive tutoring, regardless of gender or age, may register for study at any time.

3. For registration procedures, the applicant should fill in their name, gender, age, place of origin, occupation, address, whether or not they have received education, and the courses they wish to study (Civics, Mandarin Chinese, English), and attach two 2-inch half-length photos of themselves to register with the Radio Tutorial Class of the Fourth Section of this bureau. Upon registration, they will be issued a study certificate and become a student of this class.

4. The teaching subjects of the radio tutorial class are temporarily set as Civics, Mandarin Chinese, and English, which will be broadcasted separately on a regular basis.

5. The Civics course will temporarily use the Civics textbook published by Datong Bookstore. The Mandarin Chinese course will adopt the two types of "Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Textbook" (A and B) compiled by the Ministry of Education as fixed teaching materials. The English course will use flexible teaching materials, with lecturers compiling their own lectures. These lectures will be printed and distributed by the Morning Post Publishing Department commissioned by this bureau and may be published daily in the Morning Post.

6. The duration of study for the radio tutorial class is set at ten months for the first term, with six hours of instruction per week.

7. The broadcast dates for the radio tutorial class courses are specified as follows: (1) Civics: every Saturday; (2) Mandarin Chinese: every Tuesday and Thursday; (3) English: every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday. The broadcast time is set from 9:00 PM to 10:00 PM.

8. Students are responsible for purchasing the Civics and Mandarin Chinese textbooks and the English lectures themselves. This bureau will negotiate with the bookstore and newspaper office so that students can purchase or subscribe to the aforementioned textbooks, lectures, and the Morning Post at a special price upon presentation of their study certificate.

9. Upon completion of the remedial courses, the radio tutorial class students will be given a periodic performance examination by this bureau. Those who pass will be given graduation certificates to encourage them.

10. Lecturers will be appointed by this bureau to take charge of the broadcasts.

11. The broadcasting location will be at the Hainsen Company radio station on Nanjing Road in Shanghai, broadcasting at the scheduled times.

12. Matters not covered in these regulations may be amended at any time.

International Education Society's Annual Meeting to Be Held at the End of March

Visited William School Yesterday

1. The president of the Shanghai International Education Society, Mr. Kang _, has retired and returned to his country. All society affairs are temporarily handled by Mr. Li Zhaohuan, president of Jiaotong University. Yesterday afternoon, Acting President Li led more than 100 members of the society to visit the German William School on Xihui Road. Dr. Weber, Dr. Lanhua, and Dr. Kirk, principals of the school, led the visitors to tour the entire building and student-made specimens and artistic instruments. The achievements were quite remarkable. After the tour, they gathered in the school hall. Dr. Lan gave a speech, first describing the school's operation and student overview, and then lecturing on the German education system. He stated that the German school organization is different from the British one. In British schools, students' reading, games, and other activities are confined to the school, and they live with their student companions. In Germany, in addition to school education, most attention is paid to family education. Therefore, British students are less mentally stable than German students, and their development is also very different. The German education community is currently engaged in planning to produce ideal individuals. Although Germans have continental thinking, they have a very noble significance in education. After Dr. Lan's speech, the school students performed a drama, which was quite moving. Then, Acting President Li gave a thank-you speech. Finally, Mr. Baituolai, Secretary-General of the Society, reported that the annual meeting will be held at the end of March, and they also plan to visit the YMCA Middle School on Sichuan Road.

Gongshi Middle School Opened Yesterday

Gongshi Middle School officially started classes yesterday and held an opening ceremony at 8:00 AM. Attendees included Principal Cai Guojingya, as well as Guo Yicen, Li Shicen, Zhang Yaoxiang, Liu Bingli, Zhang Haishu, Zhang Liyuan, Sun Boshen, He Jia, Pan Yufeng, Luo Zhongqin, and all the students. After the ceremony, the principal, school board members, and faculty members delivered speeches respectively, reporting on the reform process and future plans, such as focusing on practical knowledge in teaching and setting up special lectures on international economics and politics. In terms of discipline, the focus will be on group-based discipline. Afterwards, a photo was taken and the event concluded.

Public Works Bureau Builds New Jingzhou Road Primary School

The Public Works Bureau has already established four primary schools for Chinese children, namely the West District Primary School on Xinzha Road, the North District Primary School on Arerjin Road, the East District Primary School on Huishan Road, and the Huade Road Primary School on Huade Road. Recently, another new primary school has been built at the corner of Huishan Road and Jingzhou Road. The school building faces south and is a three-story building with steel and concrete beams and columns, and red brick exterior walls. It is more than two hundred feet long. The south side of the building has three floors of classrooms, a total of sixteen rooms, which can accommodate 650 students. The north side of the building is a large auditorium that can accommodate 400 seats. There is a stage and equipment for projecting movies. The north wall of the auditorium is equipped with new-style movable glass windows, and outside of that, there are roll-up and roll-down blinds, all of which can be opened and closed from below with ropes, making them extremely flexible. On the east and west sides of the building, there are student cloakrooms, drinking fountains, restrooms, and classrooms. In addition, there are kindergarten rooms, science labs, art rooms, equipment rooms, kitchens, storage rooms, etc. The principal's office and the teachers' lounges for both men and women are all on the second floor. All the rooms in the building have good lighting and ventilation and are equipped with steam radiators. The school is located south of Nie Zhongcheng Public School. The area between the two schools is a common sports field, with a considerable area. The north of the field is separated by a fence, with a gate on the east and west sides. There is still extra space north of the fence, several feet wide, to be used as a primary school lawn. Swings and other play equipment will be installed on the east side of the building. The school is scheduled to open on March 1. Except for kindergarten students and first-graders, only male students will be admitted. Those who wish to send their children to study can contact Principal Jie Zhi of the Public Works Bureau's Huade Road Primary School at No. 138 Huade Road. The tuition fee is six yuan per student per semester. In addition, first-grade to third-grade students will be charged an additional three yuan per semester for books, and fourth-grade and above will be charged an additional four yuan per semester.

Donghua Wins Big Against Lancashire 6-0

Creates a Record of Sixteen Clean Sheets in Division A

Remaining Two Matches Don't Jeopardize Championship

In the Western League Division A, Donghua, with its strong strength and prestigious reputation for a hundred victories, arrived at Yiyuan yesterday and unanimously defeated Lancashire 6-0, creating a record of sixteen clean sheets. According to the schedule, with two more matches each against the Fourth Platoon and the British Army, the Division A championship is already in hand. The point of future effort is to maintain the great record of a hundred victories.

Donghua Team's Victory Was Very Easy

The Donghua team gave a full-team performance yesterday, but it was not perfect. However, compared to Lancashire, there was a world of difference. They took a casual and underestimating approach; otherwise, there might have been a better record. Zhou Xianyan was as steady as ever and can be called the number one player in Shanghai. Li Ning's leg injury has not healed, so he was much less impressive. Guan Xun'an has made great progress and has a limitless future. The center back line of Feng Yunyou, Wu Youliang, and Tu Kaiyuan was united as one, and their offense and defense were both excellent. Chen Xutian has been quite impressive recently. Wan Xianghua did not have many highlights yesterday. Chen Jiaqiu was average. Li Yichen worked hard, and Cao Qiuting was full of courage. Although it was difficult to be perfect, he felt worthy of his position. One successful kick opened the individual scoring record for this season, so he deserved to be full of smiles.

Lancashire Fought Hard and Failed

Lancashire is not a first-class team, and its fighting strength is indeed ordinary. It just happened that Donghua was in a relaxed mood, so they were able to compete with them. The center back line fought very hard, and the forwards also entered whenever there was an opening. However, the former lacked passing skills, and the latter lacked shooting power. Although there were occasional fierce attacks, they ultimately had no effect. The inside back was not positioned properly and lacked skills. The defense was just for show and had no practical effect. Whenever there was a crisis, they were flustered and panicked. If Donghua had given it their all, the loss would certainly not have been this great.

Four Goals Flowed Into the Net

Less than ten minutes into the battle, Tu Kaiyuan kicked a free kick towards the goal. The goalkeeper caught it but looked up and saw the opponent rushing in. He turned around and kicked it back in a hurry, causing everyone to laugh. Then, left and right corners. Soon after, Wu Youliang also took the ball and attacked. Li Yichen followed closely, and both he and the goalkeeper fell to the ground. The ball returned to Chen Jiaqiu's side. Chen calmly kicked it in. However, Li was still lying on the ground and had not gotten up, so the goal was ruled out because of offside. After another fifty-five minutes, the right inside back, Shi Wen, touched the ball with his hand, resulting in a penalty kick. Li Yichen kicked with his right foot, and the ball went into the net. Once the record was opened, the goals flowed in one after another. Li suddenly displayed the vigor of a dragon and tiger, broke into the enemy territory alone, and scored again within a few minutes. Cao Qiuting scored with a preemptive strike. Chen Yutian circled and advanced, taking advantage of the enemy's unpreparedness and shooting hard, hitting the right corner. After three goals, Cao also became ambitious, and like a lone army, he succeeded in winning the flag. The first half ended with four goals to zero.

Triumph After Repeatedly Breaching the Enemy's Fortress

In the second half, the enemy took advantage of the wind and attacked fiercely. Within twenty minutes, the enemy's momentum was high. Donghua's three counterattacks were unsuccessful and they retreated. At that time, although the enemy's offensive was strong, it was ultimately contained outside the inner defense line and could not enter the gate. After a long time, Feng Yunyou raised his arm and stole the ball out of bounds, handing it over to the front. Li Yichen received the order and dribbled the ball straight into the goal. Tu Kaiyuan double kicked the ball in front of the goal and was penalized with a free kick. Both sides lined up in front of the goal, facing each other. The tense situation was filled with comical fun. After the ball left the foot, both sides fought for it. Finally, Tu saved it, redeeming himself. Not long after, Wan Xianghua sent troops to the left flank, entering the battle alone and returning with merit. As a result, Donghua won the game 6-0. The referee was Pike.

Ministry of Education Approves Admission Rules for Summer Sports Training Classes

Nine admission rules for summer sports training classes of the Ministry of Education, which had been generally approved by the preparatory committee of the class a few days ago, have now been approved and promulgated by the Ministry of Education. The original text is as follows:

Admission Rules for Summer Sports Training Classes of the Ministry of Education

(1) The admission qualifications for students in this class are as follows: (1) Current sports teachers in primary and secondary schools; (2) Current staff members of public sports fields; (3) Current teachers and staff members of national martial arts halls; (4) Current personnel of educational administrative organs who handle sports administration; (5) Those who have considerable research and special interest in sports and have obtained certification from local educational administrative organs.

(2) The principle of admission for students in this class is recommendation. The recommendation methods are as follows: (1) Each provincial education department must recommend at least four people (including one teacher from primary and secondary schools and one staff member from public sports fields, and the remainder depending on local needs); (2) Each city (municipality directly under the Executive Yuan) education bureau or social bureau must recommend at least two people; (3) Each provincial and municipal national martial arts hall must recommend at least two people; (4) County and city education bureaus may, if necessary, recommend two of their own sports administration personnel or sports teachers from their affiliated schools, halls, and fields; (5) Public and private schools that have been registered may, if necessary, recommend one sports teacher from their school.

(3) Recommended students must prepare the following documents and send them by registered mail to the Preparatory Committee of the Summer Sports Training Class of the Ministry of Education in Nanjing before May 1 of this year for review: (1) Recommendation letter; (2) Registration form (format attached); (3) Two recent half-length photos.

(4) After receiving the acceptance notice from this class, the recommending organization should immediately notify the person to go to the office of this class at the National Central University at No. 4 Paifanglou, Nanjing, from July 5 to 9 to complete the following procedures: (1) Submit the acceptance notice for verification; (2) Pay the tuition fee of twenty yuan; (3) Pay the miscellaneous fee of ten yuan (for electricity, tea, printing, and other consumables); (4) Register and receive the course schedule and attendance card; (5) Those who need accommodation should collect an accommodation certificate.

(5) If students wish to have meals in the class, the class will designate a kitchen to handle it on their behalf. The monthly meal fee is tentatively set at twelve yuan, which will be handled by the students themselves. (6) Sports supplies, clothing, and other items for personal use by students must be provided by themselves.

(7) Students must not be absent from class without a good reason after entering the class. If the number of absences exceeds one-third of the total class time, they will not be allowed to participate in the examination.

(8) Upon completion of the study period, students who pass more than six-tenths of the subjects in the examination will be given a certificate with the list of subjects passed.

(9) After the examination, the Ministry will notify the recommending organizations of the students' grades.

Spring and Autumn

Preparations That the Public Should Make Before the War

— Pei Gong

丨Broadsword and Gas Mask丨

A few months ago, a scholar in England published a very insightful statement in the Manchester Guardian, titled: [Prepare for the Worst-Case Scenario]; the idea is that the Second World War will break out soon, and the world should have considerable awareness and preparation. Even the British have such thoughts. We Chinese, who are at the forefront, how exactly do we intend to deal with and prepare for the disaster that may occur immediately?

Speaking of preparation, according to my impatience, everyone can only prepare to fight desperately. Indeed, fighting desperately is the most active preparation. However, if people are unwilling to fight desperately, and cannot force the government to temporarily protect you from fighting desperately, and cannot resist, then, as a last resort, let's first make some preparations to save our own lives!

Friends, please believe me, after the war becomes more intense, the Japanese, who use killing as national education, will inevitably use [poison gas]. Therefore, we should ask scientists, doctors, and pharmacies to quickly unite to manufacture more gas masks for everyone to purchase. Secondly, to say something unlucky, perhaps in the early stages of the war, coastal areas may be trampled by the enemy, and the people may have the opportunity to fight the enemy directly. Then, preparing a broadsword and sharpening it diligently is also the least amount of preparation!

Friends, everyone should recognize that this war is a matter of life and death for us Chinese. It is better to advance and die than to retreat and die! What are we afraid of! The enemy wants us to die, and we must also teach them to die!

Eastern Mirror

— Bing Ding

| Exposed |

The threshold of a matter has already become clear; the darkness of a matter has already been unveiled; this is called [Exposing the Eastern Mirror]. Generally, Chinese people have simple minds and dull eyes. When they see the tricks of foreigners, they find them incredibly strange, like microscopes and telescopes, and are amazed by them as if they were the work of gods and demons. There are also some Jianghu (江湖, itinerant entertainers) friends who set up a box on the streets and in villages, using convex lenses to magnify the pictures inside, attracting children from the streets to gather and watch. The scenery, dramas, wars, and colorful scenes captivate the audience. Finally, there are also mysterious, fleeting glimpses of erotic pictures, which especially make the audience's minds wander. Therefore, this kind of Eastern Mirror still exists everywhere today, becoming a profession for Jianghu friends. In fact, the scenery is photography; the dramas are paper paintings; as for the "Spring in the Han Palace", everyone has their own good performances. So, to expose it, this kind of Eastern Mirror has no viewing value at all.

All things in the world should be viewed in this way: for example, women, with their myriad charms, who dares to have frivolous thoughts? But modern young ladies may be used to being embraced by men on the dance floor; the concubines in mansions and the "vases" in counters may be the backbone of the human flesh market. Therefore, once the Eastern Mirror is exposed, their worth is no longer noble. The great figures in political, academic, and business circles are the same; seen from afar, they are truly awe-inspiring, with imposing airs and full of airs, who doesn't lose courage upon seeing them? In fact, once the Eastern Mirror is exposed, they not only turn into paper tigers, but may even be worse than dogs and horses, truly making people laugh their teeth off.

The Eastern Japanese country was originally one of the world's five major powers; annexing Korea, swallowing Taiwan, ceding Ryukyu, and defeating strong Russia. Their playing of the Eastern Mirror was truly lively, playing one after another, never playing a tragedy. Since the September 18th Incident, they seized Fanyang without leaving a single arrow, and later completely swallowed Manchuria. Fearing that the audience in the world would have a negative reaction, they played a puppet show in the Eastern Mirror. Now that the Eastern Mirror has been completely exposed, the audience in the world is rising up to boo, but it shamelessly continues. Since the Songhu Battle, we Chinese have taken the lead in the first 回敎 (Muslim?) one, and the Eastern Mirror they played has long been exposed; after changing several commanders, they still cannot defeat our 19th Route Army. Moreover, on the bodies of the captured soldiers, they found talismans with [Taishang Laojun, hurry, hurry, as the law commands, decree!], as well as diaries fearing war and death. Isn't this exposing the Eastern Mirror? We Chinese have always only known how to expose Western Mirrors; now, let's all rise up and [Expose the Eastern Mirror]!

New Spring Outfits

— Fang Xuelu

Street Artists

— Huo Xueming

| Clay Figurine Makers |

Under low eaves, in narrow alleys with small painted walls, or in quiet areas of factories: we can find street artists.

Don't think that only the poets, musicians, painters, architects, and all the great talents serving the court are worthy of being called artists. In this era, the old die and the new are born. The breath of the laborers of Wall Street is music, the conversation of blacksmiths is poetry, and those who can create imagist paintings are worthy of being called painters. Of course, the title of architect should not be monopolized by the drafters alone, but every carpenter and mason who participates in the construction of a house is an architect. Because artists should indeed use their brains, but they must also use their strength at the same time.

Furthermore, you must also know that so-called works of art are not just poems, songs, paintings, dramas, architecture, etc. To find works of art with modern light, one should have this kind of understanding. Let me introduce you to street artists:

Isn't that right? An old Jiangbei man wearing a blue cloth village outfit, with a long beard and hair, looks a bit like Tolstoy: he also doesn't brush his teeth, and his clothes are covered with snot and dirt, and also looks like [unruly] Wang Anshi or modern national scholar Zhang Taiyan; he is definitely not a lazy person. He spends his life faithfully cultivating his confident skills. Starting from the morning, he leaves his poor home, carrying a pole, and embarks on the journey of art. Where there are many children, he puts down his pole.

An artist especially sings and praises the pure innocence of children. Everyone's life is most comfortable and peaceful only when listening to their mother's lullaby in the cradle. And so it is with street artists. He smiles when he sits in front of the children. He opens his pole, takes out flour or sugar, and with his hands, he creates green parrots, red-faced Guan Yu, and statues of Indians with red cloth wrapped around their heads. If you ask him to make a tumbler or a swordsman or a martial woman, they are all lifelike. Although these skilled works also have their ups and downs, they have inevitably inconsistent achievements just like literary works and musical scores that are created by each writer. We cannot say that these flour or sugar models are not works of art because of inherited contemporary concepts, just as we cannot deny that Greek and Italian sculptures and famous European shadow figures (Shadow Figure) are works of art. For the same reason, and to express the lively symbols of modern radical social life, it is not the beauty of classicism, but the beauty of rough power. Facing the paintings of the modern German Fauvist school and the Futurist literary movement, I am even more convinced of my theory.

These street artists sell their works cheaply to children, and their treatment in China is just like that of literati selling their manuscripts, living a miserable life.

Novel

The Landlord

— Qin Shouou

[Good]! The landlord jumped up like a fierce tiger, his eyes as big as copper bells. [Elder brother, second brother,... you take thirty people to resist for a while!] He pointed the tip of his knife at the people who were called, and they immediately started walking. Behind them, six pure yellow fierce dogs roared like tigers, their tails like iron rods, vying to follow their masters and bravely rush to the enemy.

The sound of people and dogs running immediately stirred up a tense atmosphere.

[Fifth brother, Xiaoling, Xiaohe, hurry up and prepare bows and arrows!] The landlord also dispatched the second batch of soldiers and generals; this was to prepare for the worst, in case the front line could not hold and had to retreat to defend the village. The landlord had two good horses, which he personally brought back from the north in his middle age; in the previous two [wars against the Japanese pirates], they had also made great contributions of blood and sweat. At this time, two long-term workers had already led them to the square. The horses also seemed to understand their master's intentions, knowing that they were about to go into battle, and they all raised their manes and neighed loudly.

Because they had already undergone two training sessions, every long-term worker in the landlord's family had a heart as big as a bucket. The second batch of reinforcements did not need the landlord's deployment, and had already rushed out with the third brother.

The third brother was the most valiant of the landlord's seven sons. He had once used a horse and a spear to repel three hundred Japanese pirates; and once, he was shot in the forehead by a Japanese pirate's arrow, and the blood dyed his pale yellow face a deep red. He still fought bravely and did not retreat. In the end, he forcefully pulled out the arrow and reflected it back, using it to shoot and kill a Japanese pirate captain.

[Landlord! The Japanese pirates are strong, they can't resist them, half of the thirty people are already dead!]

Just as the landlord was about to mount his horse and prepare to personally meet the enemy, the second alarm came. [Where have the Japanese pirates reached?] The old man calmly took off his coat and inserted a short sword diagonally on his back.

[They are about to enter the village!] An unexpected report. (Four)

The Paradise of Women

Sitting Postures and Psychological Speculation

— Wanzhen

I was sitting opposite Zhang Xiaozu, and I said to her: "I don't know why you are so absent-minded."

"I'm very worried, but:" she said, looking at me, and then asked.

"What do you mean by what you said?"

I told her: "I was paying attention to your sitting posture." I knew she would definitely want to understand, so I continued to briefly tell her:

I can guess your thoughts from the posture of your legs when you sit. For example! If you sit with your legs apart, but your toes are turned inwards, as in the first picture, it means you are very bored, either you are daydreaming, or you are definitely absent-minded.

Sitting like this, the legs are definitely not arranged very neatly, and not just any sitting will result in this posture. Just pay attention and when that person sits like this, you can ask her, and let her say whether this is the case. (She might jump up after hearing this).

Many people sit with their legs very close together. Like the second picture, this posture seems too heavy. At that time, that person's mind must be very clear, and their thinking is also quick; at that time, they must be very disciplined, and seem to be sitting upright with an inviolable air.

Many people sit with their legs one in front of the other, as in the third picture. This posture seems to be deep in thought, or it implies the leisurely attitude of a poet.

Some people lean back on the chair, half-lying and half-sitting, with one leg over the other, as in the fourth picture. This person's posture seems too casual.

Of course, it cannot be said that everyone is like this, this is just speculation based on the postures of most people.

Women's short coats (see explanation on Sunday)

Free Talk

The So-called [Explanation]

— Li Shui

I am not afraid of great figures killing people at will, I am only afraid of great figures coming up with an [explanation] after killing someone! A tiger eats a sheep, and that's the end of it; but people, after eating people, have to make themselves out to be benevolent and righteous, and describe the person being eaten as utterly evil, never to be restored. This is truly terrifying.

Humans, not just Chinese people, all have a bit of a mentality of worshiping great figures. The weak can say ten or a hundred times without attracting attention; a great figure only needs to fart, and it will cause a stir. For example, in ancient times, if the emperor did something wrong, wrongly killed someone, if the emperor himself did not think it was wrong, naturally everyone would have nothing to say; if he said he had done something wrong and expressed remorse, then those ministers and scholars would immediately sing praises to the emperor's sagacity, giving it their all. As for the wrongly done thing and the wrongly killed person, it would naturally be right to be wrong, and there would be nothing more to say. However, this is only something that the emperor can do. If it is a great figure of the second rank, then they must [explain]!

The methods of [explanation] are various: doing a good job of covering up, burying incriminating evidence, and directly announcing the [truth] (?) of why the person was killed in order to gain the understanding of the people of the world, one way; calling a deer a horse, reversing black and white, making the world's eyes dazzled and unable to distinguish right from wrong, a second way; if the situation is dangerous, such as in the modern era with a strong flavor of democracy, where the actions of great figures are often criticized by young people who do not understand affairs, great figures, in order to evade those vicious gazes, can [explain] to even greater great figures, and then have the [great great figures] come out to [explain] to the people, a third way.

The Japanese occupation of the Northeast is already enough to break our hearts; but when we hear the Japanese in the League of Nations speaking of their benevolent and righteous [explanation] of [developing the rich resources of the Northeast for the Chinese people] [driving away the warlords and eliminating internal strife for the Chinese people!], doesn't it make us feel even more heartbroken?

XXXXXXX, after shooting XXXX, was subjected to condemnation by pens. It is reported that on X month X day, he has already [explained] to the XXXX great great figure. I am really worried about how that great great figure will [explain] to the people on behalf of that Chairman, I think it will be: [The official is wise, the slave deserves it]!

Alas, the dead are gone, what about the living? [A good head, who will chop it off?] I hope everyone will feel their own necks!

Twilight Jottings

— Qian Gechuan

We work for others for a day, and at the time when day and night intersect, we lazily run home wanting to sleep but not sleeping, and instead pick up a cigarette. Cigarettes are exciting, everyone knows that. In the twilight, leaning on the railing and blowing a couple of puffs of smoke, even I, who am not a poet, feel the loveliness of this leisure time. Raising my head, I see the vast sky, and lowering my head, I see the shadowy figures of people. All fantasies are built up from this half-light. I then want to take advantage of this time of all things to think as much as possible, to think of all the things that I could not get during the day. However, before I could see that happiest of lives, it was already broken by the lamp of reason. My current situation has no happiness, only one human head after another, sparsely walking by. In my ears, it seems as if there is a voice ringing: [Don't fantasize! Fantasizing is suffering for yourself!] At this time, I am completely awake. Wherever my eyes reach, there is a Western-style head of a man without a hat. His hair is like a newly cut piece of black satin, so smooth that it can be used as a mirror. I suddenly realize that everyone else is wearing a hat, but he alone is not wearing one, he must not want to hide the beauty of his hair. Chinese women don't wear hats either, probably for the same reason. Western-style heads are all parted on the left, supposedly starting from Napoleon. Because Napoleon had a scar on his right skull, he combed his hair from the left to cover it. The world did not know the inside story, and all said that it looked good combed this way, so it became the standard of beauty.

Going downstairs and strolling on the street, as soon as I go out, I see some wild chickens expressing their love to the men passing by. This is a live drama that happens every evening in Shanghai. I don't want to watch it, and continue to walk forward. A rickshaw came shouting from behind, with a very wealthy woman sitting on it. It walked in front of me, less than thirty feet away, when suddenly, with an "aiya" sound, the rickshaw puller stepped on a banana peel and fell to the ground, and the wealthy woman also tumbled off the rickshaw, her silk cheongsam torn. The woman lay on the ground, scolded the rickshaw puller a few words, and then suddenly began to cry loudly. The passersby all gathered around, and I also joined in to watch the excitement. I only heard the woman crying and complaining. At first, she wanted the rickshaw puller to compensate her for the clothes. Later, knowing that the rickshaw puller couldn't afford to pay, she could only blame heaven: [Heaven! Why did you have to tear my going-out clothes? What will I wear to the factory tomorrow? I worked for three years to make this one piece of clothing, and I don't have a penny now!] Those people on the road who were wearing gorgeous clothes all sighed in unison. Only a middle-aged woman wearing cloth clothes, without saying a word, generously took out a five-yuan banknote from her pocket and handed it to her, saying: [Take this and make a piece of cloth clothing] to wear.

The audience dispersed, and I still walked forward. In the distance, I saw a store, with bright electric lights. Walking closer, I realized that it was W·C Bookstore. Because its business was thriving, it had just moved to a larger store and was selling at special prices. Stores go from big to small, and book prices go from expensive to cheap. The facts before my eyes show us that they have made money no matter what. But I always feel a little strange in my heart, thinking: Is what Mr. Xu said last night false? He clearly said that W·C Bookstore lost tens of thousands of dollars and is about to close down now. To make money, they have to sell at large discounts, which may be a commercial tactic of small profits but quick turnover; but to move to a big store when they are about to close down, this I can't understand no matter what!

In the Tram

— Yuru

It was a clear and peaceful early spring evening, and the setting sun weakly reflected on the sidewalk on the left side of Diksui Road. I came out of the YWCA, dragging my long, thin shadow toward the tram stop on North Sichuan Road. I was planning to take the tram to the Hai Ge Road Sanatorium to visit a friend. After waiting for a long time, I finally jumped onto a tram with an unexpectedly crowded number of passengers. In the car, besides myself and a short and very fat lady with a strong Cantonese accent, there were only men. Because it was in a third-class car, and it was so crowded, there was naturally no hope of a seat, so I stood on the platform outside the car without wanting to go inside. When the car arrived at Bazilu, several people wanted to get off, and the ticket seller asked me to squeeze in, so I squeezed in. Order was greatly disrupted, and the men who were standing all turned their heads to stare at you without hesitation. Although a lot of people got off, it seemed that not a few people got on either. Your body was still under severe pressure. I don't know where that fat lady was squeezed to.

"Let you sit!" Suddenly a hand landed on my arm. It was a young man in a suit sitting next to the price list.

"Thank you!" I sat down without hesitation. He then stood in front of me. Knees against knees, often rubbing uncomfortably due to the swaying of the car, which made people very uncomfortable, but what could I do? He let me sit down. Gradually, this very frequent contact became constant, and then he simply fixed you in place and didn't move, and then sandwiched your knees between his hard legs, so that you couldn't move at all.

"It's really crowded!" I pulled my leg out and said angrily.

"That's right, it's really annoying, so many people!" He widened the gap a little.

The car slid down from the Waibaidu Bridge, and many boats were crowded on the Suzhou River.

At one point, I thought of a small book in my pocket, so I took it out and looked at it, flipping through the illustrations one by one. Finally, when I saw the "Autumn on the Edogawa River" by the painter Fujita, a foreign sentiment floated vaguely in my heart. Suddenly, the fingers of the hand holding the book received a strange sensation, as if they had been electrocuted, and I quickly retracted them. "You can sit, please! Annoying!" I stood up abruptly in the crowd with glaring eyes, and my face turned hot. The passengers' gazes involuntarily turned to the young man at the same time. Some were very suspicious, and some seemed to have quite a bit of experience, expressing an attitude of "of course that's the way it is" and cracking their mouths.

When he reached Rixinlou, the poor thing got off the car leisurely. He maintained a calm attitude throughout.

The Black Woman's Search for God (XI)

— Written by Xiao Boner, translated by Yi Xian

She handed the cup back to him, and he made it disappear as if he were a sorcerer, so she laughed, and he laughed too. "It's so clever, sir," she said. "You are a great magician. You are probably instructing the black woman in something. I am looking for God. Where is he?"

"Inside you," the sorcerer said. "And inside me."

"I think so too," the girl said. "But what is he?"

"He is our father," said the sorcerer.

The black girl made a face, thought for a while, and then said, "Why not our mother?"

Then it was the sorcerer's turn to make a face, and he made a face like this. "Our mothers want us to bring them before God," he said. "If I had always been guided by my mother, then I would probably be rich, not a vagrant, a wanderer. But then I would not have seen God either."

"My father beat me from a young age, until I was big enough to resist him with my [Norbo] Kelly]," said the black girl; "Even after that, he wanted to sell me to a white soldier gentleman who had crossed the sea after leaving his wife. I have never said, Our Father who art in heaven,] I always say [Our Grandfather]. I don't want a God who is my father."

"We should still love each other like brothers and sisters," the sorcerer said with a smile; because the amendment of grandfather touched his comical sense. Moreover, he was an amiable person, and always laughed when something was funny.

"Women don't love brothers," said the black girl. "A woman's heart turns from her brothers to strangers, as my heart turns to you."

"Oh! Let's not talk about family: it's just a metaphor," said the sorcerer. "We are members of the same human society, and it can be said that I am your member and you are mine. As for family, let's just leave it be."

"I can't, sir," she said. "God told me that he doesn't care about individuals, sisters, and brothers, etc." "This is just a way of teaching us to love each other," said the sorcerer. "Love those who hate you. Bless those who curse you. Never forget that two blacks cannot become one white."

"I don't want everyone to love me," said the black girl. "I can't love everyone. God told me that I cannot use my [Norbo] Kelly] to beat them simply because I hate people, and that whenever people hate me, their hatred of me cannot give them the right to beat me. But God has made me hate many. There are a group of people who, because they plunder and kill others, are like snakes and must be killed."

"You still shouldn't remind me of this group of people," said the sorcerer. "This group of people makes me very unhappy."

"Forgetting unhappy things is indeed a way to make everything wonderful," said the black girl. "But it doesn't make everything credible; make everything appropriate. But do you really, truly love me, sir?"

Words from a Thatched Cottage

— Zizhan

(9) Short and Zhu Zhensheng

During last year's Songhu Anti-Japanese War, six Japanese planes bombed Suzhou. The American aviator Short took off to fight, but unfortunately, his lone plane was surrounded and he was killed. This tragic event is still remembered by the Chinese people. Who knew that thirty years ago, when war between Japan and Russia was imminent and the situation in China was extremely dangerous, a German named Zhu Zhensheng committed suicide to inspire the Chinese?

Zhu Zhensheng lived in China for thirty years, spoke Chinese, wore Chinese clothes, and used a Chinese name. He served as the chief instructor of artillery at Jiangning, Zhenjiang, Jiangyin, and Wusong, dedicating himself to Chinese national affairs. When the conflict between Japan and Russia over the three northeastern provinces arose, he was distressed by China's inadequacy and constantly unhappy, especially angry at the Russians. He traveled to Shanghai and met a Russian, questioning him about the three northeastern provinces and accusing the Russians of mistreating China and violating justice. The Russian laughed and replied, "Do you think there's still hope for China? Why worry so much about it?" Zhu became even more angry upon hearing this. He asked an Englishman to mediate the affairs of the three northeastern provinces, but the Englishman gave him the same answer as the Russian. Zhu was furious, appearing almost insane. Upon returning to Jiangning and seeing Chinese people, he would shake their hands and tell them about the suffering of China's future and the urgency of reform. The Chinese responded carelessly, and some even mocked him. One day, at a Western restaurant, he spoke of the three northeastern provinces with clenched teeth and glaring eyes, smashing his cups and plates. The next day, he prepared to leave with a gun, but bystanders stopped him. He returned, closed the door, and committed suicide. As he was dying, he repeatedly shouted, "China cannot be saved! China cannot be saved!" When the servants opened the door to check on him, they found a piece of paper on the table, stating, "Zhu's suicide has nothing to do with China. Germans must not use this as an excuse to make trouble for the Chinese." Such was his concern for our China!

Inconsistent Rise and Fall of Public Bonds

丨No Trading on the 27th Due to Settlement丨

There were no transactions in April contracts, so there was no room for maneuver. The prices of the remaining bonds fell by varying amounts of 3 to 5 jiao due to selling of the 11th and 34th bonds. The second session was peaceful, with slight fluctuations of 1 to 2 jiao. The unified salt tax still rose by 5 fen to 2 jiao and 5 fen due to differences in supply and demand. US Cotton Soft Due to Economic Decline

New York, February 24: A report on the cotton market for the week states that the cotton market price rose this week due to the Smith Cotton Act, which aims to reduce cotton production this year, being passed in the Senate. However, it soon rebounded, and the market has been unsettled recently. The reason for this is the weakness in the securities market, and the financial and economic situation in the United States is also worrying. The first delivery notice for the March contract was for approximately 42,000 bales. The Cotton Exchange Communication Agency estimates that there were 2,863,000 bales of cotton on the cotton market at the end of January this year, compared to 3,919,000 bales at the same time last year and 1,839,000 bales at the same time the year before last. However, those holding spot goods seem quite confident. Sales in the South were very low this week. The regulations issued by the Ministry of Agriculture to manage this year's cotton production loans limit individual loans to 300 yuan, with the condition of reducing cotton fields in three. Some in the industry do not believe that this method will be effective in reducing the total amount of cotton fields. The House of Representatives committee reviewing the Smith Cotton Act was satisfied, but whether it will become law is still questionable, as it is expected that some in the House of Representatives will oppose it. Grain and Rice Market Situation

Yin Yuan Rice Price Rises by 12 Cents

(Shanghai South) Yesterday, the source of rice was blocked, and the supply of early rice was completely absent. Both retail and wholesale markets were sluggish. Although there was no new supply, the market remained stable. Few rice merchants from Suzhou, Tongxiang, Qingjiao, and Nangang were present, and prices did not fluctuate much. The price of Du Jian rice remained stable. Yin Yuan rice was scarce and popular. For example, in Songjiang, the price of Yin Yuan rice rose by 20 cents per dan (unit of weight). The movement of Bian Yuan rice was sluggish, and the price slightly decreased.

(Shanghai North) Yesterday, there was a lack of supply from the river. There were only 130 to 140 boats in the river. White粳 rice shops continued to sell, and the market was generally stable, with a slight increase for medium-grade rice. There was very little Bo粳 early rice in the river, and the price showed a tightening trend. The movement of Yangbu Jian rice was normal, and the price remained stable. | Nanjing Xian Rice Continues to Arrive in Shanghai |

Yesterday, the sales of native Xian rice were still mainly in the local market. This Month's Flour Market is Soft and Declining

| Distant Months Slightly Higher |

Yesterday, the flour market was stable in the morning for each month, with the price of foreign wheat rising by about 10 cents. Outsiders were concerned because the situation was becoming more serious. Large and small factories had no intention to sell, so the market was relatively stable amid mutual avoidance. Factories also hedged against the possibility of problems with the supply of foreign wheat in the future, and standards would inevitably be affected. Therefore, everyone acted cautiously. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading was still light. Because the end of the month was approaching, and deliveries were due, factories had plenty of chips. Only the Jin merchants and Tianjin merchants moved slightly, so prices naturally softened. The prices of distant months were generally fluctuating, and both insiders and outsiders adopted a wait-and-see attitude, with no intention to enter or exit the market. However, there were very few sellers, and the market was slightly higher. As a result, this month's price fell by 7.5 li (unit of currency, 1/1000 of a yuan) compared to the previous day, March remained unchanged, April rose by 5 li, May and June rose by 7.5 li, and July remained unchanged.

One-Fen Steel Plate Jumps Up by More Than 6 Qian

The English steel plate market originally had the potential to improve due to the small amount of goods arriving and the high prices. It is also said that overseas prices recently reached 7 pounds and 15 shillings, so local prices are unlikely to fall in the short term.

War Situation Unfolds in the Lingnan Area

No Major Changes on Various Fronts

Japanese Troops Advance to Attack Taipingfang, Outflanking Chaoyang

Dong's Troops Build Strong Fortifications Northwest of Chaoyang

Our Troops Cover the Evacuation of People from Counties in the War Zone

Over 1,000 Rebel Troops in Kailu Disarmed by Cui's Troops

(Beiping) 10,000 Japanese infantry and 5,000 cavalry are advancing towards Lingnan. The vanguard troops made formal contact with our troops on the evening of the 24th. Because of the flat terrain of Chaoyang and Kailu, which is difficult to defend, we are focusing our efforts on Lingnan, Lingyuan, and northward to Chifeng and Jianping. It is expected that the Japanese troops will advance steadily, and the main battle will be on the Lingyuan-Chifeng line. Our troops are in high spirits and are prepared to fight to the death. However, there is a shortage of food supplies in the area. Tang Yulin has sent a telegram requesting assistance from all parties. (26th Dispatch)

(Beiping) A telegram from Qinhuangdao at 10:00 AM on the 25th stated that at dawn today, approximately 20,000 Japanese and rebel troops secretly crossed Shaomao Mountain and launched a fierce attack on our positions east of Laoye Temple. Our artillery team set up artillery at Heishan, taking advantage of the high ground. The enemy's aircraft began bombing our positions at noon. The British Consulate was severely bombed, and the casualties among residents were incalculable. At around 3:00 PM, the majority of the Japanese and rebel troops advanced from Baimiao, Yaowangmiao, and Zengjiafen, with the rebel troops acting as the vanguard and traitors as guides. After our troops resisted with all their might, they ultimately failed to succeed. Currently, there are no changes on the Lingnan front. (26th Dispatch) (Tianjin) A telegram from Rehe stated that more than 20 enemy aircraft bombed Chaoyang, Lingnan, and other places on the morning of the 26th. Our troops have covered the evacuation of the people from Chaoyang, Fuxin, Suidong, Kailu, and other counties and have advanced to new defensive lines to resist. Enemy and rebel reinforcements are rapidly advancing. (26th Dispatch)

(Beiping) A telegram from Chengde on the evening of the 25th stated that the fierce battle in the Chaoyang area lasted for seven hours, and the enemy did not gain an inch. The road from Lingyuan to Chaoyang is guarded by our troops at every point. (26th Dispatch)

(Beiping) A telegram from Chengde at 11:00 PM on the 25th stated that the rebel troops of Wang Weiqing's unit, under Japanese cover, advanced towards Kailu. After being surrounded by Cui's troops on three sides, over 1,000 rebel troops were disarmed by us at Aigen Temple, and a Mongolian staff officer of Zhang Hai peng was captured. According to his confession, the Japanese army planned to advance into the plains and deserts with 300 armored vehicles. We are on strict guard. (26th Dispatch)

(Beiping) According to foreign news, after changes in our troop formations in Kailu, our regular army has dispatched reinforcements from Chifeng to intercept and engage them. A fierce battle is underway. Last night, puppet troops were discovered in Beiliang attempting to sneak in across the mountains. They were defeated by Liu's battalion of Tang's troops, with many captured and killed or wounded. Because the Japanese troops attempted to attack from the east of Chaoyang, crossing the mountains, but failed to succeed, they concentrated their forces this morning and attacked Taipingfang from Wujiazi, outflanking Chaoyang. Dong's troops have built strong fortifications in the northwest of Chaoyang. (26th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Tang Yulin telegraphed Ping claiming that, according to reports from the front, three aircraft have been reconnoitering in Xiawa for several consecutive days. Three more aircraft came on the 25th and dropped three bombs, which were repelled by Feng Zhanhai's volunteer army without causing any casualties. Lubei is extremely safe. Kailu seems to have other developments, and Chaoyang is in a state of emergency. Infantry and artillery units have been sent to advance towards the front lines. (26th Dispatch)

(Beiping) Cui, the commander of Kailu, reported at 11:00 PM on the 24th that more than 3,000 infantry, cavalry, and artillery troops of the Japanese 39th Division in Tongliao, supported by armored vehicles, artillery, and aircraft, attacked our left wing in the Fengsanjiazi area. Zhang Haipeng's advance unit engaged in fierce fighting with Zhang's regiment of our front-line troops. After failing to attack Kailu twice, the enemy, in order to avoid casualties, used Zhang's unit as the vanguard, with only one Japanese artillery team placed at the vanguard and the 39th and 34th Divisions responsible for the left and right flanks. Zhang Haipeng's rebel troops totaled 12,000 men. At 2:00 AM, the artillery fire was intense. Our side replaced the new defensive lines, and the battle had not stopped at the time of the telegram. (25th Dispatch)

(Beiping) When someone questioned a certain figure in Chinese military circles about the Japanese claim that Japanese troops had occupied Chaoyang, that figure replied that this was a familiar trick of the Japanese to fabricate and exaggerate victories according to their pre-determined plans. Yesterday, we received an official report from Chaoyang dated the morning of the 25th, stating that everything was peaceful and quiet, and there had been no fighting. There have been no subsequent reports since then, probably because there was nothing to report. The Beiping Telegraph Bureau still received a telegram from Chaoyang last night, which included a statement that there was no trace of the enemy at the front, indicating that the area had not been occupied by Japanese troops. He Zhuguo, the commander of the Chinese army in Qinhuangdao, received news from the front last night that there was a fierce battle in Lingnan. Two brigades of the Chinese army were holding key passes in a good defensive position, resisting the attack of 20,000 Japanese and Manchu troops. (26th Reuters Dispatch)

Suzuki Brigade Pressures Chaoyang

(Beiping) The Japanese troops attacking Rehe issued a general offensive order on all fronts this morning. The Suzuki Brigade attacking Chaoyang has been pressuring Chaoyang. The Dong Futing Brigade stationed there made contact with the enemy at Yangniuyingzi and Baiyaoziguo Jiachapeng in the east of Chaoyang the day before yesterday, and the battle was extremely fierce. This time, the Japanese army launched a large-scale general offensive, which included five battalions of Zhang Haipeng's puppet infantry and four battalions of cavalry, as well as the Hiraga Brigade dispatched from Heilongjiang. (26th Dispatch)

Kailu City Suffers Heavy Bombing

(Beiping) Kailu City has been bombed by Japanese aircraft for several consecutive days. The county government and public security bureau have been destroyed, and the county magistrate has gone missing. Enemy troops are still increasing and launching fierce attacks on Chaoyang via Raoyang County. Our troops are putting up strong resistance and are still in fierce fighting. (26th Dispatch)

The Impact of Shao Benliang's Defection

(Beiping) Huang Pichen, director of the Rehe office in Beiping, said that the Japanese army has launched another attack on Chaoyang. Our front-line troops, Dong's brigade, have been resisting with all their might for several times. The rebel army Shao Benliang was originally a Rehe soldier. He was bribed by the Japanese side and defected, and he is familiar with our situation, which has had a considerable impact on our battle in Beipiao. (26th Dispatch)

Japanese Troops in Yuguan Seem to Have Intentions of Attacking Westward

(Beiping) Japanese troops in Yuguan seem to have intentions of attacking westward. Enemy aircraft were discovered conducting reconnaissance on the front line of Shihe this morning. (26th Dispatch)

Volunteer Army in Jiamusi Captures Enemy Artillery Positions

(Beiping) Last month, Yang Shouxu's volunteer army engaged in a fierce battle with Japanese troops in Jiamusi for several days, with heavy casualties on both sides. Later, Yang's army formed a suicide squad of hundreds of men, armed with broadswords and grenades, and launched a fierce and brave charge, breaking through the enemy's positions. The entire enemy artillery unit was annihilated, and six field guns, six mountain guns, and twelve machine guns were captured. At the end of January, after the enemy had completed reinforcements, they forced Yang's army back to the positions. Yang's broadsword suicide squad launched a charge, and the enemy could not withstand it. The enemy artillery all knelt on the ground, holding red and white talismans, and tearfully begged for mercy. The enemy artillery, except for those who were killed, were all captured. (25th Dispatch)

Popular Sentiment in Beiping is Stirring

(Beiping) Popular sentiment in Beiping is very good, and there is a unanimous call for resistance. Even children are supporting the government and donating money to purchase "Children's Aircraft" to aid in the war effort. It is also reported that the singing girls in Beiping are now organizing fundraising groups to raise money to purchase aircraft. News reporters who are going to the front lines to observe the war are all riding horses, wearing fur coats, and carrying luggage, entering this mountainous and rugged Rehe Province, which is reminiscent of travel in the previous century. (26th Reuters Dispatch)

Volunteer Army in Jilin Province Prepares to Attack Harbin

(Beiping) The Jilin volunteer army, part of Yang Zhibin's force, is stationed in three locations. Guo's brigade and other units, totaling over 7,000 men, are currently stationed east of Bin County. Luo's brigade and other units, totaling over 7,000 men, are currently stationed in Wuchang County. Wang's brigade, totaling over 3,000 men, is lurking around Changchun. On the 12th, Guo's brigade occupied Feiguangtu in Bin County and attacked Jiabantong and other places. Taking advantage of the emptiness of the Japanese and rebel forces in Harbin and Changchun, they are concentrating their forces and launching a large-scale attack on Harbin, coordinating with other units and preparing to act simultaneously. (25th Dispatch)

And Pile Sandbags to Build Defenses

Japanese Transport Ships Unload Large Quantities of Military Supplies

(Tianjin) According to a telephone report from Tanggu, the Japanese garrison in the area is building underground tunnels inside the barracks, strictly prohibiting Chinese people from spying on them. It is not known where the tunnels lead to. It is speculated that their purpose is related to the railway station. Japanese troops in the area have recently stepped up their vigilance, sending out many sentries at night, prohibiting pedestrians, and creating a tense situation. Sandbags have been piled up to build defenses in many places. The other day, the Yuguchi Maru transport ship arrived from Lushun carrying large quantities of military supplies, all of which were rifles and bombs. (26th Dispatch)

Patriotic Young Man Drowns Himself in the Sea

A Suicide Note with Extremely Tragic Words

(Tianjin) According to people from Yangliuqing Town, there was a man named Zhang Enhong in the town, 23 years old, living in Youfang Alley. He was a handsome young man with an extraordinary temperament. Since the September 18th Incident, he had gone to the Northeast twice, but had not fulfilled his ambition to resist Japan and save the country. On January 19th of this year, he went to Qingdao to visit his cousin Dai Ziliang, seeking work to save the country. Dai was the captain of a warship in the Northeast Fleet, but there was no opportunity. Every time they discussed the Northeast Incident, he would regret it all day long. On January 27th, Dai's warship was ordered to leave, and he advised Zhang to return home. Zhang remained silent and immediately went out and drowned himself in the sea. The next day, his body was washed up on the beach by the tide. Four suicide notes were found on his body, wrapped in oiled paper. The words were extremely tragic, roughly stating that China was in danger, Japan was hateful, and he hoped that the Chinese people would unite and quickly save the country. Dai has telegraphed his family to go to Qingdao to transport the coffin. (26th Dispatch)

National Committee Member Xu Shaozhen Plans Not to Hold an Inauguration Ceremony

(Nanjing) The newly appointed National Committee Member Xu Shaozhen, due to a foot ailment that makes it difficult for him to walk, has obtained the consent of Chairman Lin not to hold an inauguration ceremony.
